Particularly the narrative of the "[New Frontier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Frontier)" has been criticized as unreflected continuation of [settler colonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Settler_colonialism) and [manifest destiny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifest_destiny), continuing the narrative of exploration as fundamental to the assumed [human nature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_nature).[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Schaberg_2021-159)[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Renstrom_2021-160)[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Haskins-149)[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-DNLee-154)[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Drake-150) Joon Yun considers [space colonization as a solution to human survival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_and_survival) and global problems like pollution to be imperialist;[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-161) others have identified space as a new [sacrifice zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacrifice_zone) of colonialism.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Calma_2021-162)

[Natalie B. Trevino](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Natalie_B._Trevino&action=edit&redlink=1) argues that not colonialism but [coloniality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decoloniality) will be carried into space if not reflected on.[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Filling_Space_2021-163)[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Trevino_2021-164)

More specifically the advocacy for territorial colonization [of Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_colonization) opposed to [habitation in the atmospheric space of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_colonization) has been called *surfacism*,[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Tickle_2015-165)[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-166) a concept similar to [Thomas Golds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Gold) [*surface chauvinism*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface_chauvinism).

More generally space infrastructure such as the [Mauna Kea Observatories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mauna_Kea_Observatories) have also been [criticized and protested against](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_to_the_Mauna_Kea_Observatories) as being colonialist.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Matson_Nunn_2021-167) [Guiana Space Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre) has also been the site of anti-colonial protests, connecting colonization as an issue on Earth and in space.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Durrani_2019-98)

In regard to the scenario of [extraterrestrial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_contact_(science_fiction)) [first contact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_contact_(anthropology)) it has been argued that the employment of colonial language would endanger such first impressions and encounters.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Bartels_2018h-152)

Furthermore spaceflight as a whole and space law more particularly has been criticized as a postcolonial project by being built on a colonial legacy and by not facilitating the sharing of access to space and its benefits, too often allowing spaceflight to be used to sustain colonialism and imperialism, most of all on Earth instead.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Durrani_2019-98)

### **Planetary protection**

*See also: [Planetary protection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_protection)*

Robotic spacecraft to Mars are required to be sterilized, to have at most 300,000 spores on the exterior of the craft—and more thoroughly sterilized if they contact "special regions" containing water, or it could contaminate life-detection experiments or the planet itself.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-groundwatercontamination-168)[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-COSPAR_PLANETARY_PROTECTION_POLICY-169)

It is impossible to sterilize human missions to this level, as humans are host to typically a hundred trillion [microorganisms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microorganism) of thousands of species of the [human microbiome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_microbiome), and these cannot be removed while preserving the life of the human. Containment seems the only option, but it is a major challenge in the event of a hard landing (i.e. crash).[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-biospherescollide-170) There have been several planetary workshops on this issue, but with no final guidelines for a way forward yet.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-171) Human explorers could also inadvertently contaminate Earth if they return to the planet while carrying extraterrestrial microorganisms.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-172)

### **Physical, mental and emotional health risks to colonists**

*Main article: [Effect of spaceflight on the human body](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effect_of_spaceflight_on_the_human_body)*

The health of the humans who may participate in a colonization venture would be subject to increased physical, mental and emotional risks. [NASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA) learned that – without gravity – bones lose [minerals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mineral_(nutrient)), causing [osteoporosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteoporosis).[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-173) [Bone density](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bone_density) may decrease by 1% per month,[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-nasa-body-174) which may lead to a greater risk of osteoporosis-related fractures later in life. Fluid shifts towards to the head may cause vision problems.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-175) NASA found that isolation in closed environments aboard the [International Space Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station) led to [depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)), [sleep disorders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep_disorder), and diminished personal interactions, likely due to confined spaces and the monotony and boredom of long space flight.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-nasa-body-174)[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-176) [Circadian rhythm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circadian_rhythm) may also be susceptible to the effects of space life due to the effects on sleep of disrupted timing of sunset and sunrise.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-weir-177) This can lead to exhaustion, as well as other sleep problems such as [insomnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insomnia), which can reduce their productivity and lead to mental health disorders.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-weir-177) High-energy radiation is a health risk that colonists would face, as radiation in deep space is deadlier than what astronauts face now in low Earth orbit. Metal shielding on space vehicles protects against only 25-30% of space radiation, possibly leaving colonists exposed to the other 70% of radiation and its short and long-term health complications.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-:0-178)

## Implementation

Building colonies in space would require access to water, food, space, people, construction materials, energy, transportation, [communications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication), [life support](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_support_system), [simulated gravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simulated_gravity), [radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiation) protection, migration, governance and capital investment. It is likely the colonies would be located near the necessary physical resources. The practice of [space architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_architecture) seeks to transform spaceflight from a heroic test of human endurance to a normality within the bounds of comfortable experience. As is true of other frontier-opening endeavors, the capital investment necessary for space colonization would probably come from governments,[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-179) an argument made by John Hickman[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-180) and [Neil deGrasse Tyson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_deGrasse_Tyson).[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-181)

### **Migration**

[Human spaceflight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_spaceflight) has enabled only temporarily relocating few privileged people and no permanent space migrants.

The society and motivation for space migration has been questioned as rooted in colonialism, questioning the fundamentals and inclusivity of space colonization. Highlighting the need to reflect on such socio-economic issues beside the technical challenges for implementation.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-m794-182)

### **Governance**

A range of different models of transplanetary or extraterrestrial governance have been sketched or proposed. Often envisioning the need for a fresh or idenpendent extraterrestrial governance, particularly in the void left by the contemporarily critizised lacking space governance and inclusivity.

It has been argued that space colonialism would, similarly to terrestrial [settler colonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Settler_colonialism), produce colonial national identities.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Eller_2022_pp._148%E2%80%93160-183)

### **Life support**

*Further information: [Effect of spaceflight on the human body](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effect_of_spaceflight_on_the_human_body), [Space medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_medicine), and [Space food](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_food)*

> 
> 
> 
> Depiction of [NASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA)'s plans to grow food on [Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars)
> 

In space settlements, a life support system must recycle or import all the nutrients without "crashing." The closest terrestrial analogue to space life support is possibly that of a [nuclear submarine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_submarine). Nuclear submarines use mechanical life support systems to support humans for months without surfacing, and this same basic technology could presumably be employed for space use. However, nuclear submarines run "open loop"—extracting oxygen from seawater, and typically dumping [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide) overboard, although they recycle existing oxygen.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-184)Another commonly proposed life-support system is a [closed ecological system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Closed_ecological_system)such as [Biosphere 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biosphere_2).[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-185)

### **Solutions to health risks**

*See also: [Bioastronautics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioastronautics)*

Although there are many physical, mental, and emotional health risks for future colonists and pioneers, solutions have been proposed to correct these problems. [Mars500](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars500), [HI-SEAS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HI-SEAS), and SMART-OP represent efforts to help reduce the effects of loneliness and confinement for long periods of time. Keeping contact with family members, celebrating holidays, and maintaining cultural identities all had an impact on minimizing the deterioration of mental health.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-186) There are also health tools in development to help astronauts reduce anxiety, as well as helpful tips to reduce the spread of germs and bacteria in a closed environment.[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-187) Radiation risk may be reduced for astronauts by frequent monitoring and focusing work away from the shielding on the shuttle.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-:0-178) Future space agencies can also ensure that every colonist would have a mandatory amount of daily exercise to prevent degradation of muscle.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-:0-178)

### **Radiation protection**

*See also: [Health threat from cosmic rays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_threat_from_cosmic_rays)*

[Cosmic rays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_rays) and [solar flares](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_flare) create a lethal radiation environment in space. In orbit around certain planets with magnetospheres (including Earth), the [Van Allen belts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_Allen_belts)make living above the atmosphere difficult. To protect life, settlements must be surrounded by sufficient mass to absorb most incoming radiation, unless magnetic or plasma radiation shields were developed.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-spacecraftshielding-188) In the case of Van Allen belts, these could be drained using orbiting tethers[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-mirnov1996-189) or radio waves.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-190)

Passive mass shielding of four metric tons per square meter of surface area will reduce radiation dosage to several [mSv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sievert#Yearly_dose_examples) or less annually, well below the rate of some populated [high natural background areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Background_radiation#Natural_background_radiation) on Earth.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-191) This can be leftover material (slag) from processing lunar soil and asteroids into oxygen, metals, and other useful materials. However, it represents a significant obstacle to manoeuvring vessels with such massive bulk (mobile spacecraft being particularly likely to use less massive active shielding).[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-spacecraftshielding-188) Inertia would necessitate powerful thrusters to start or stop rotation, or electric motors to spin two massive portions of a vessel in opposite senses. Shielding material can be stationary around a rotating interior.

### **Psychological adjustment**

The monotony and loneliness that comes from a prolonged space mission can leave astronauts susceptible to cabin fever or having a psychotic break. Moreover, lack of sleep, fatigue, and work overload can affect an astronaut's ability to perform well in an environment such as space where every action is critical.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-192)

### **Economics**

Space colonization can roughly be said to be possible when the necessary methods of space colonization become [cheap enough](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_behavior) (such as space access by cheaper launch systems) to meet the cumulative funds that have been gathered for the purpose, in addition to estimated profits from [commercial use of space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_use_of_space).[[*citation needed*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed)]

Although there are no immediate prospects for the large amounts of money required for space colonization to be available given traditional launch costs,[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-193)there is some prospect of a radical reduction to launch costs in the 2010s, which would consequently lessen the cost of any efforts in that direction. With a published price of US$56.5 million per launch of up to 13,150 kg (28,990 lb) payload[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-sxCapabilitiesSvcs20131211-194) to [low Earth orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit), [SpaceX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX) [Falcon 9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falcon_9) rockets are already the "cheapest in the industry".[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-fp20131209-195) Advancements currently being developed as part of the [SpaceX reusable launch system development program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX_reusable_launch_system_development_program) to enable reusable Falcon 9s "could drop the price by an order of magnitude, sparking more space-based enterprise, which in turn would drop the cost of access to space still further through economies of scale."[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-fp20131209-195) If SpaceX is successful in developing the reusable technology, it would be expected to "have a major impact on the cost of access to space", and change the increasingly [competitive market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Competition_(economics)) in space launch services.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-bbc20130930-196)

The [President's Commission on Implementation of United States Space Exploration Policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President%27s_Commission_on_Implementation_of_United_States_Space_Exploration_Policy) suggested that an [inducement prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inducement_prize_contest) should be established, perhaps by government, for the achievement of space colonization, for example by offering the prize to the first organization to place humans on the Moon and sustain them for a fixed period before they return to Earth.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-197)

### **Money and currency**

Experts have debated on the possible usage of money and currencies in societies that will be established in space. The Quasi Universal Intergalactic Denomination, or QUID, is a physical currency made from a space-qualified polymer [PTFE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polytetrafluoroethylene) for inter-planetary travelers. QUID was designed for the foreign exchange company Travelex by scientists from Britain's National Space Centre and the University of Leicester.[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-198)

Other possibilities include the incorporation of [cryptocurrency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptocurrency) as the primary form of currency, as suggested by [Elon Musk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk).[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-199)

### **Resources**

*Further information: [Asteroid mining](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid_mining)*

Colonies on the Moon, Mars, asteroids, or the metal-rich planet [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet)), could extract local materials. The Moon is deficient in [volatiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volatile_(astrogeology)) such as [argon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argon), [helium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helium) and compounds of [carbon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon), [hydrogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrogen) and [nitrogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen). The LCROSS impacter was targeted at the Cabeus crater which was chosen as having a high concentration of water for the Moon. A plume of material erupted in which some water was detected. Mission chief scientist Anthony Colaprete estimated that the Cabeus crater contains material with 1% water or possibly more.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-200) Water [ice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice) should also be in other permanently shadowed craters near the lunar poles. Although helium is present only in low concentrations on the Moon, where it is deposited into [regolith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regolith) by the solar wind, an estimated million tons of He-3 exists over all.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-201) It also has industrially significant [oxygen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen), [silicon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicon), and metals such as [iron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron), [aluminum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aluminum), and [titanium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titanium).

Launching materials from Earth is expensive, so bulk materials for colonies could come from the Moon, a [near-Earth object](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Near-Earth_object) (NEO), [Phobos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phobos_(moon)), or [Deimos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deimos_(moon)). The benefits of using such sources include: a lower gravitational force, no [atmospheric drag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drag_(physics)) on cargo vessels, and no biosphere to damage. Many NEOs contain substantial amounts of metals. Underneath a drier outer crust (much like [oil shale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_shale)), some other NEOs are inactive comets which include billions of tons of water ice and [kerogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerogen)hydrocarbons, as well as some nitrogen compounds.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-202)

Farther out, [Jupiter's Trojan asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonization_of_the_outer_Solar_System#Jupiter_trojans) are thought to be rich in water ice and other volatiles.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-203)

[Recycling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recycling) of some raw materials would almost certainly be necessary.

### **Energy**

[Solar energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_energy) in orbit is abundant, reliable, and is commonly used to power satellites today. There is no night in free space, and no clouds or atmosphere to block sunlight. Light intensity obeys an [inverse-square law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverse-square_law). So the solar energy available at distance *d* from the Sun is *E* = 1367/*d*2 W/m2, where *d* is measured in [astronomical units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_unit) (AU) and 1367 watts/m2 is the energy available at the distance of Earth's orbit from the Sun, 1 AU.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-204)

In the weightlessness and vacuum of space, high temperatures for industrial processes can easily be achieved in [solar ovens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_ovens) with huge parabolic reflectors made of metallic foil with very lightweight support structures. Flat mirrors to reflect sunlight around radiation shields into living areas (to avoid line-of-sight access for cosmic rays, or to make the Sun's image appear to move across their "sky") or onto crops are even lighter and easier to build.

Large solar power photovoltaic cell arrays or thermal power plants would be needed to meet the electrical power needs of the settlers' use. In developed parts of Earth, electrical consumption can average 1 kilowatt/person (or roughly 10 [megawatt-hours](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watt-hour) per person per year.)[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-205) These power plants could be at a short distance from the main structures if wires are used to transmit the power, or much farther away with [wireless power transmission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wireless_power_transmission).

A major export of the initial space settlement designs was anticipated to be large [solar power satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_power_satellite) (SPS) that would use wireless power transmission (phase-locked [microwave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microwave) beams or lasers emitting wavelengths that special solar cells convert with high efficiency) to send power to locations on Earth, or to colonies on the Moon or other locations in space. For locations on Earth, this method of getting power is extremely benign, with zero emissions and far less ground area required per watt than for conventional solar panels. Once these satellites are primarily built from lunar or asteroid-derived materials, the price of SPS electricity could be lower than energy from fossil fuel or nuclear energy; replacing these would have significant benefits such as the elimination of [greenhouse gases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_gases) and [nuclear waste](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_waste)from electricity generation.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-206)

Transmitting solar energy wirelessly from the Earth to the Moon and back is also an idea proposed for the benefit of space colonization and energy resources. Physicist Dr. David Criswell, who worked for NASA during the Apollo missions, came up with the idea of using power beams to transfer energy from space. These beams, microwaves with a wavelength of about 12 cm, will be almost untouched as they travel through the atmosphere. They can also be aimed at more industrial areas to keep away from humans or animal activities.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-i2massociates.com-207) This will allow for safer and more reliable methods of transferring solar energy.

In 2008, scientists were able to send a 20 watt microwave signal from a mountain in Maui to the island of Hawaii.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-208) Since then [JAXA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JAXA) and Mitsubishi has teamed up on a $21 billion project in order to place satellites in orbit which could generate up to 1 gigawatt of energy.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-209) These are the next advancements being done today in order to make energy be transmitted wirelessly for space-based solar energy.

However, the value of SPS power delivered wirelessly to other locations in space will typically be far higher than to Earth. Otherwise, the means of generating the power would need to be included with these projects and pay the heavy penalty of Earth launch costs. Therefore, other than proposed demonstration projects for power delivered to Earth,[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-NatSecSpaceOffice2007-210) the first priority for SPS electricity is likely to be locations in space, such as communications satellites, fuel depots or "orbital tugboat" boosters transferring cargo and passengers between [low Earth orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit) (LEO) and other orbits such as [geosynchronous orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geosynchronous_orbit) (GEO), [lunar orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_orbit) or [highly-eccentric Earth orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highly_elliptical_orbit) (HEEO).[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Lewis1997-211): 132  The system will also rely on satellites and receiving stations on Earth to convert the energy into electricity. Because of this energy can be transmitted easily from dayside to nightside meaning power is reliable 24/7.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-212)

[Nuclear power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power) is sometimes proposed for colonies located on the Moon or on Mars, as the supply of solar energy is too discontinuous in these locations; the Moon has nights of two Earth weeks in duration. Mars has nights, relatively high gravity, and an atmosphere featuring [large dust storms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_of_Mars#Effect_of_dust_storms) to cover and degrade solar panels. Also, Mars' greater distance from the Sun (1.52 astronomical units, AU) means that only *1/1.522* or about 43% of the solar energy is available at Mars compared with Earth orbit.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-213) Another method would be transmitting energy wirelessly to the lunar or Martian colonies from solar power satellites (SPSs) as described above; the difficulties of generating power in these locations make the relative advantages of SPSs much greater there than for power beamed to locations on Earth. In order to also be able to fulfill the requirements of a Moon base and energy to supply life support, maintenance, communications, and research, a combination of both nuclear and solar energy will be used in the first colonies.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-i2massociates.com-207)

For both solar thermal and nuclear power generation in airless environments, such as the Moon and space, and to a lesser extent the very thin Martian atmosphere, one of the main difficulties is dispersing the [inevitable heat generated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnot_cycle). This requires fairly large radiator areas.

### **Self-replication**

*See also: [von Neumann probe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_probe), [Self-replicating machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-replicating_machine), and [molecular nanotechnology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_nanotechnology)*

[Space manufacturing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_manufacturing) could enable self-replication. Some consider it the ultimate goal because it would allow an [exponential](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exponential_growth) increase in colonies, while eliminating costs to and dependence on Earth.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-214) It could be argued that the establishment of such a colony would be Earth's first act of [self-replication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-replication).[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-215) Intermediate goals include colonies that expect only information from Earth (science, engineering, entertainment) and colonies that just require periodic supply of light weight objects, such as [integrated circuits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrated_circuit), medicines, [genetic material](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA) and tools.

### **Population size**

In 2002, the [anthropologist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthropology) [John H. Moore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_H._Moore) estimated[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-216) that a population of 150–180 would permit a stable society to exist for 60 to 80 generations—equivalent to 2,000 years.

Assuming a journey of 6,300 years, the astrophysicist Frédéric Marin and the particle physicist Camille Beluffi calculated that the minimum viable population for a [generation ship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generation_ship) to reach [Proxima Centauri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxima_Centauri) would be 98 settlers at the beginning of the mission (then the crew will breed until reaching a stable population of several hundred settlers within the ship) .[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-217)[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-218)

In 2020, Jean-Marc Salotti proposed a method to determine the minimum number of settlers to survive on an extraterrestrial world. It is based on the comparison between the required time to perform all activities and the working time of all human resources. For Mars, 110 individuals would be required.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-219)

## Advocacy

*See also: [Space advocacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_advocacy)*

Several private companies have announced plans toward the [colonization of Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonization_of_Mars). Among entrepreneurs leading the call for space colonization are [Elon Musk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk), [Dennis Tito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dennis_Tito) and [Bas Lansdorp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bas_Lansdorp).[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-220)[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-221)

## Criticisms

Space colonization has been seen as a relief to the problem of [human overpopulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_overpopulation) as early as 1758,[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-tsr2009-137) and listed as one of Stephen Hawking's reasons for pursuing space exploration.[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-138) Critics note, however, that a slowdown in population growth rates since the 1980s has alleviated the risk of overpopulation.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-tsr2009-137)

Critics also argue that the costs of commercial activity in space are too high to be profitable against Earth-based industries, and hence that it is unlikely to see significant exploitation of space resources in the foreseeable future.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Marshall-139)

Other objections include concerns that the forthcoming colonization and [commodification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commodification) of the cosmos is likely to enhance the interests of the already powerful, including major economic and military institutions e.g. the large financial institutions, the major aerospace companies and the [military–industrial complex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military%E2%80%93industrial_complex), to lead to new [wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War), and to exacerbate pre-existing exploitation of [workers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exploitation_of_labour) and [resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exploitation_of_natural_resources), [economic inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_inequality), [poverty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poverty), [social division](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_division) and [marginalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_exclusion), environmental degradation, and other detrimental processes or institutions.[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Dickens-MR-2010-11-7)[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Dickens-MR-2008-02-8)[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Dickens-MR-2017-03-9)

Additional concerns include creating a culture in which humans are no longer seen as human, but rather as material assets. The issues of [human dignity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_dignity), [morality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morality), [philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy), [culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture), [bioethics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioethics), and the threat of megalomaniac leaders in these new "societies" would all have to be addressed in order for space colonization to meet the [psychological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychological) and [social](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_(sociology)) needs of people living in isolated colonies.[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-140)

As an alternative or addendum for the future of the human race, many science fiction writers have focused on the realm of the 'inner-space', that is the computer-aided exploration of the [human mind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_mind) and human [consciousness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness)—possibly en route developmentally to a [Matrioshka Brain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matrioshka_Brain).[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-141)

[Robotic spacecraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotic_spacecraft) are proposed as an alternative to gain many of the same scientific advantages without the limited mission duration and high cost of life support and return transportation involved in human missions.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-142)

A corollary to the [Fermi paradox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_paradox)—"nobody else is doing it"[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-143)—is the argument that, because no evidence of [alien colonization technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_paradox#Alien_constructs)[[*broken anchor*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MOS:BROKENSECTIONLINKS)] exists, it is statistically unlikely to even be possible to use that same level of technology ourselves.[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-144)

### **Colonialism**

*See also: [Manifest destiny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifest_destiny), [Space advocacy § Decolonizing space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_advocacy#Decolonizing_space), [Space ethics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_ethics), [Ethics of terraforming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethics_of_terraforming), and [Planetary chauvinism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_chauvinism)*

> 
> [Gemini 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gemini_5) mission badge (1965) connecting spaceflight to colonial endeavours[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Roger_Launiuss_Blog_2011-145)

> ![%E2%AD%90%EF%B8%8F%20SpaceRAG%20Text%201c747df749744da19743ce68743431af/image122.png](%E2%AD%90%EF%B8%8F%20SpaceRAG%20Text%201c747df749744da19743ce68743431af/image122.png)

> The logo and name of the [Lunar Gateway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Gateway) references the [St. Louis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis) [Gateway Arch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gateway_Arch),[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-146)which some see as associating Mars with the [American frontier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_frontier)and the [*manifest destiny*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifest_destiny)mentality of [American settler colonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Settler_colonialism#Settler_colonialism_in_the_United_States).[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-NPR.org_2015-147)
> 

Space colonization has been discussed as [postcolonial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Postcolonialism)[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Durrani_2019-98) continuation of [imperialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialism) and [colonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonialism),[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-148)[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Haskins-149)[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Drake-150)[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-marshall-151) calling for [decolonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decolonization) instead of colonization.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Bartels_2018h-152)[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-NatGeo_2018-153)Critics argue that the present politico-legal regimes and their philosophic grounding advantage imperialist development of space,[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-marshall-151)that key decisionmakers in space colonization are often wealthy elites affiliated with private corporations, and that space colonization would primarily appeal to their peers rather than ordinary citizens.[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-DNLee-154)[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-155) Furthermore, it is argued that there is a need for inclusive[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-156) and democratic participation and implementation of any space exploration, infrastructure or habitation.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Tavares_Buckner_Burton_McKaig_2020-157)[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-158)According to space law expert Michael Dodge, existing [space law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_law), such as the [Outer Space Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_Space_Treaty), guarantees access to space, but does not enforce social inclusiveness or regulate non-state actors.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Bartels_2018h-152)

Particularly the narrative of the "[New Frontier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Frontier)" has been criticized as unreflected continuation of [settler colonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Settler_colonialism) and [manifest destiny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifest_destiny), continuing the narrative of exploration as fundamental to the assumed [human nature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_nature).[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Schaberg_2021-159)[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Renstrom_2021-160)[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Haskins-149)[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-DNLee-154)[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Drake-150) Joon Yun considers [space colonization as a solution to human survival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_and_survival) and global problems like pollution to be imperialist;[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-161) others have identified space as a new [sacrifice zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacrifice_zone) of colonialism.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Calma_2021-162)

[Natalie B. Trevino](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Natalie_B._Trevino&action=edit&redlink=1) argues that not colonialism but [coloniality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decoloniality) will be carried into space if not reflected on.[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Filling_Space_2021-163)[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Trevino_2021-164)

More specifically the advocacy for territorial colonization [of Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_colonization) opposed to [habitation in the atmospheric space of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_colonization) has been called *surfacism*,[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Tickle_2015-165)[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-166) a concept similar to [Thomas Golds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Gold) [*surface chauvinism*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface_chauvinism).

More generally space infrastructure such as the [Mauna Kea Observatories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mauna_Kea_Observatories) have also been [criticized and protested against](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_to_the_Mauna_Kea_Observatories) as being colonialist.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Matson_Nunn_2021-167) [Guiana Space Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre) has also been the site of anti-colonial protests, connecting colonization as an issue on Earth and in space.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Durrani_2019-98)

In regard to the scenario of [extraterrestrial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_contact_(science_fiction)) [first contact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_contact_(anthropology)) it has been argued that the employment of colonial language would endanger such first impressions and encounters.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Bartels_2018h-152)

Furthermore spaceflight as a whole and space law more particularly has been criticized as a postcolonial project by being built on a colonial legacy and by not facilitating the sharing of access to space and its benefits, too often allowing spaceflight to be used to sustain colonialism and imperialism, most of all on Earth instead.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Durrani_2019-98)

### **Planetary protection**

*See also: [Planetary protection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_protection)*

Robotic spacecraft to Mars are required to be sterilized, to have at most 300,000 spores on the exterior of the craft—and more thoroughly sterilized if they contact "special regions" containing water, or it could contaminate life-detection experiments or the planet itself.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-groundwatercontamination-168)[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-COSPAR_PLANETARY_PROTECTION_POLICY-169)

It is impossible to sterilize human missions to this level, as humans are host to typically a hundred trillion [microorganisms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microorganism) of thousands of species of the [human microbiome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_microbiome), and these cannot be removed while preserving the life of the human. Containment seems the only option, but it is a major challenge in the event of a hard landing (i.e. crash).[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-biospherescollide-170) There have been several planetary workshops on this issue, but with no final guidelines for a way forward yet.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-171) Human explorers could also inadvertently contaminate Earth if they return to the planet while carrying extraterrestrial microorganisms.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-172)

### **Physical, mental and emotional health risks to colonists**

*Main article: [Effect of spaceflight on the human body](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effect_of_spaceflight_on_the_human_body)*

The health of the humans who may participate in a colonization venture would be subject to increased physical, mental and emotional risks. [NASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA) learned that – without gravity – bones lose [minerals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mineral_(nutrient)), causing [osteoporosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteoporosis).[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-173) [Bone density](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bone_density) may decrease by 1% per month,[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-nasa-body-174) which may lead to a greater risk of osteoporosis-related fractures later in life. Fluid shifts towards to the head may cause vision problems.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-175) NASA found that isolation in closed environments aboard the [International Space Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station) led to [depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)), [sleep disorders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep_disorder), and diminished personal interactions, likely due to confined spaces and the monotony and boredom of long space flight.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-nasa-body-174)[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-176) [Circadian rhythm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circadian_rhythm) may also be susceptible to the effects of space life due to the effects on sleep of disrupted timing of sunset and sunrise.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-weir-177) This can lead to exhaustion, as well as other sleep problems such as [insomnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insomnia), which can reduce their productivity and lead to mental health disorders.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-weir-177) High-energy radiation is a health risk that colonists would face, as radiation in deep space is deadlier than what astronauts face now in low Earth orbit. Metal shielding on space vehicles protects against only 25-30% of space radiation, possibly leaving colonists exposed to the other 70% of radiation and its short and long-term health complications.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-:0-178)

## Implementation

Building colonies in space would require access to water, food, space, people, construction materials, energy, transportation, [communications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication), [life support](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_support_system), [simulated gravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simulated_gravity), [radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiation) protection, migration, governance and capital investment. It is likely the colonies would be located near the necessary physical resources. The practice of [space architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_architecture) seeks to transform spaceflight from a heroic test of human endurance to a normality within the bounds of comfortable experience. As is true of other frontier-opening endeavors, the capital investment necessary for space colonization would probably come from governments,[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-179) an argument made by John Hickman[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-180) and [Neil deGrasse Tyson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_deGrasse_Tyson).[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-181)

### **Migration**

[Human spaceflight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_spaceflight) has enabled only temporarily relocating few privileged people and no permanent space migrants.

The society and motivation for space migration has been questioned as rooted in colonialism, questioning the fundamentals and inclusivity of space colonization. Highlighting the need to reflect on such socio-economic issues beside the technical challenges for implementation.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-m794-182)

### **Governance**

A range of different models of transplanetary or extraterrestrial governance have been sketched or proposed. Often envisioning the need for a fresh or idenpendent extraterrestrial governance, particularly in the void left by the contemporarily critizised lacking space governance and inclusivity.

It has been argued that space colonialism would, similarly to terrestrial [settler colonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Settler_colonialism), produce colonial national identities.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Eller_2022_pp._148%E2%80%93160-183)

### **Life support**

*Further information: [Effect of spaceflight on the human body](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effect_of_spaceflight_on_the_human_body), [Space medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_medicine), and [Space food](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_food)*

> 
> 
> 
> Depiction of [NASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA)'s plans to grow food on [Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars)
> 

In space settlements, a life support system must recycle or import all the nutrients without "crashing." The closest terrestrial analogue to space life support is possibly that of a [nuclear submarine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_submarine). Nuclear submarines use mechanical life support systems to support humans for months without surfacing, and this same basic technology could presumably be employed for space use. However, nuclear submarines run "open loop"—extracting oxygen from seawater, and typically dumping [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide) overboard, although they recycle existing oxygen.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-184)Another commonly proposed life-support system is a [closed ecological system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Closed_ecological_system)such as [Biosphere 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biosphere_2).[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-185)

### **Solutions to health risks**

*See also: [Bioastronautics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioastronautics)*

Although there are many physical, mental, and emotional health risks for future colonists and pioneers, solutions have been proposed to correct these problems. [Mars500](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars500), [HI-SEAS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HI-SEAS), and SMART-OP represent efforts to help reduce the effects of loneliness and confinement for long periods of time. Keeping contact with family members, celebrating holidays, and maintaining cultural identities all had an impact on minimizing the deterioration of mental health.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-186) There are also health tools in development to help astronauts reduce anxiety, as well as helpful tips to reduce the spread of germs and bacteria in a closed environment.[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-187) Radiation risk may be reduced for astronauts by frequent monitoring and focusing work away from the shielding on the shuttle.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-:0-178) Future space agencies can also ensure that every colonist would have a mandatory amount of daily exercise to prevent degradation of muscle.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-:0-178)

### **Radiation protection**

*See also: [Health threat from cosmic rays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_threat_from_cosmic_rays)*

[Cosmic rays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_rays) and [solar flares](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_flare) create a lethal radiation environment in space. In orbit around certain planets with magnetospheres (including Earth), the [Van Allen belts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_Allen_belts)make living above the atmosphere difficult. To protect life, settlements must be surrounded by sufficient mass to absorb most incoming radiation, unless magnetic or plasma radiation shields were developed.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-spacecraftshielding-188) In the case of Van Allen belts, these could be drained using orbiting tethers[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-mirnov1996-189) or radio waves.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-190)

Passive mass shielding of four metric tons per square meter of surface area will reduce radiation dosage to several [mSv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sievert#Yearly_dose_examples) or less annually, well below the rate of some populated [high natural background areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Background_radiation#Natural_background_radiation) on Earth.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-191) This can be leftover material (slag) from processing lunar soil and asteroids into oxygen, metals, and other useful materials. However, it represents a significant obstacle to manoeuvring vessels with such massive bulk (mobile spacecraft being particularly likely to use less massive active shielding).[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-spacecraftshielding-188) Inertia would necessitate powerful thrusters to start or stop rotation, or electric motors to spin two massive portions of a vessel in opposite senses. Shielding material can be stationary around a rotating interior.

### **Psychological adjustment**

The monotony and loneliness that comes from a prolonged space mission can leave astronauts susceptible to cabin fever or having a psychotic break. Moreover, lack of sleep, fatigue, and work overload can affect an astronaut's ability to perform well in an environment such as space where every action is critical.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-192)

### **Economics**

Space colonization can roughly be said to be possible when the necessary methods of space colonization become [cheap enough](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_behavior) (such as space access by cheaper launch systems) to meet the cumulative funds that have been gathered for the purpose, in addition to estimated profits from [commercial use of space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_use_of_space).[[*citation needed*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed)]

Although there are no immediate prospects for the large amounts of money required for space colonization to be available given traditional launch costs,[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-193)there is some prospect of a radical reduction to launch costs in the 2010s, which would consequently lessen the cost of any efforts in that direction. With a published price of US$56.5 million per launch of up to 13,150 kg (28,990 lb) payload[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-sxCapabilitiesSvcs20131211-194) to [low Earth orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit), [SpaceX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX) [Falcon 9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falcon_9) rockets are already the "cheapest in the industry".[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-fp20131209-195) Advancements currently being developed as part of the [SpaceX reusable launch system development program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX_reusable_launch_system_development_program) to enable reusable Falcon 9s "could drop the price by an order of magnitude, sparking more space-based enterprise, which in turn would drop the cost of access to space still further through economies of scale."[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-fp20131209-195) If SpaceX is successful in developing the reusable technology, it would be expected to "have a major impact on the cost of access to space", and change the increasingly [competitive market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Competition_(economics)) in space launch services.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-bbc20130930-196)

The [President's Commission on Implementation of United States Space Exploration Policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President%27s_Commission_on_Implementation_of_United_States_Space_Exploration_Policy) suggested that an [inducement prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inducement_prize_contest) should be established, perhaps by government, for the achievement of space colonization, for example by offering the prize to the first organization to place humans on the Moon and sustain them for a fixed period before they return to Earth.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-197)

### **Money and currency**

Experts have debated on the possible usage of money and currencies in societies that will be established in space. The Quasi Universal Intergalactic Denomination, or QUID, is a physical currency made from a space-qualified polymer [PTFE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polytetrafluoroethylene) for inter-planetary travelers. QUID was designed for the foreign exchange company Travelex by scientists from Britain's National Space Centre and the University of Leicester.[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-198)

Other possibilities include the incorporation of [cryptocurrency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptocurrency) as the primary form of currency, as suggested by [Elon Musk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk).[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-199)

### **Resources**

*Further information: [Asteroid mining](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid_mining)*

Colonies on the Moon, Mars, asteroids, or the metal-rich planet [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet)), could extract local materials. The Moon is deficient in [volatiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volatile_(astrogeology)) such as [argon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argon), [helium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helium) and compounds of [carbon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon), [hydrogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrogen) and [nitrogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen). The LCROSS impacter was targeted at the Cabeus crater which was chosen as having a high concentration of water for the Moon. A plume of material erupted in which some water was detected. Mission chief scientist Anthony Colaprete estimated that the Cabeus crater contains material with 1% water or possibly more.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-200) Water [ice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice) should also be in other permanently shadowed craters near the lunar poles. Although helium is present only in low concentrations on the Moon, where it is deposited into [regolith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regolith) by the solar wind, an estimated million tons of He-3 exists over all.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-201) It also has industrially significant [oxygen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen), [silicon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicon), and metals such as [iron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron), [aluminum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aluminum), and [titanium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titanium).

Launching materials from Earth is expensive, so bulk materials for colonies could come from the Moon, a [near-Earth object](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Near-Earth_object) (NEO), [Phobos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phobos_(moon)), or [Deimos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deimos_(moon)). The benefits of using such sources include: a lower gravitational force, no [atmospheric drag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drag_(physics)) on cargo vessels, and no biosphere to damage. Many NEOs contain substantial amounts of metals. Underneath a drier outer crust (much like [oil shale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_shale)), some other NEOs are inactive comets which include billions of tons of water ice and [kerogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerogen)hydrocarbons, as well as some nitrogen compounds.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-202)

Farther out, [Jupiter's Trojan asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonization_of_the_outer_Solar_System#Jupiter_trojans) are thought to be rich in water ice and other volatiles.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-203)

[Recycling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recycling) of some raw materials would almost certainly be necessary.

### **Energy**

[Solar energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_energy) in orbit is abundant, reliable, and is commonly used to power satellites today. There is no night in free space, and no clouds or atmosphere to block sunlight. Light intensity obeys an [inverse-square law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverse-square_law). So the solar energy available at distance *d* from the Sun is *E* = 1367/*d*2 W/m2, where *d* is measured in [astronomical units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_unit) (AU) and 1367 watts/m2 is the energy available at the distance of Earth's orbit from the Sun, 1 AU.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-204)

In the weightlessness and vacuum of space, high temperatures for industrial processes can easily be achieved in [solar ovens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_ovens) with huge parabolic reflectors made of metallic foil with very lightweight support structures. Flat mirrors to reflect sunlight around radiation shields into living areas (to avoid line-of-sight access for cosmic rays, or to make the Sun's image appear to move across their "sky") or onto crops are even lighter and easier to build.

Large solar power photovoltaic cell arrays or thermal power plants would be needed to meet the electrical power needs of the settlers' use. In developed parts of Earth, electrical consumption can average 1 kilowatt/person (or roughly 10 [megawatt-hours](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watt-hour) per person per year.)[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-205) These power plants could be at a short distance from the main structures if wires are used to transmit the power, or much farther away with [wireless power transmission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wireless_power_transmission).

A major export of the initial space settlement designs was anticipated to be large [solar power satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_power_satellite) (SPS) that would use wireless power transmission (phase-locked [microwave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microwave) beams or lasers emitting wavelengths that special solar cells convert with high efficiency) to send power to locations on Earth, or to colonies on the Moon or other locations in space. For locations on Earth, this method of getting power is extremely benign, with zero emissions and far less ground area required per watt than for conventional solar panels. Once these satellites are primarily built from lunar or asteroid-derived materials, the price of SPS electricity could be lower than energy from fossil fuel or nuclear energy; replacing these would have significant benefits such as the elimination of [greenhouse gases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_gases) and [nuclear waste](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_waste)from electricity generation.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-206)

Transmitting solar energy wirelessly from the Earth to the Moon and back is also an idea proposed for the benefit of space colonization and energy resources. Physicist Dr. David Criswell, who worked for NASA during the Apollo missions, came up with the idea of using power beams to transfer energy from space. These beams, microwaves with a wavelength of about 12 cm, will be almost untouched as they travel through the atmosphere. They can also be aimed at more industrial areas to keep away from humans or animal activities.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-i2massociates.com-207) This will allow for safer and more reliable methods of transferring solar energy.

In 2008, scientists were able to send a 20 watt microwave signal from a mountain in Maui to the island of Hawaii.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-208) Since then [JAXA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JAXA) and Mitsubishi has teamed up on a $21 billion project in order to place satellites in orbit which could generate up to 1 gigawatt of energy.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-209) These are the next advancements being done today in order to make energy be transmitted wirelessly for space-based solar energy.

However, the value of SPS power delivered wirelessly to other locations in space will typically be far higher than to Earth. Otherwise, the means of generating the power would need to be included with these projects and pay the heavy penalty of Earth launch costs. Therefore, other than proposed demonstration projects for power delivered to Earth,[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-NatSecSpaceOffice2007-210) the first priority for SPS electricity is likely to be locations in space, such as communications satellites, fuel depots or "orbital tugboat" boosters transferring cargo and passengers between [low Earth orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit) (LEO) and other orbits such as [geosynchronous orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geosynchronous_orbit) (GEO), [lunar orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_orbit) or [highly-eccentric Earth orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highly_elliptical_orbit) (HEEO).[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Lewis1997-211): 132  The system will also rely on satellites and receiving stations on Earth to convert the energy into electricity. Because of this energy can be transmitted easily from dayside to nightside meaning power is reliable 24/7.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-212)

[Nuclear power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power) is sometimes proposed for colonies located on the Moon or on Mars, as the supply of solar energy is too discontinuous in these locations; the Moon has nights of two Earth weeks in duration. Mars has nights, relatively high gravity, and an atmosphere featuring [large dust storms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_of_Mars#Effect_of_dust_storms) to cover and degrade solar panels. Also, Mars' greater distance from the Sun (1.52 astronomical units, AU) means that only *1/1.522* or about 43% of the solar energy is available at Mars compared with Earth orbit.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-213) Another method would be transmitting energy wirelessly to the lunar or Martian colonies from solar power satellites (SPSs) as described above; the difficulties of generating power in these locations make the relative advantages of SPSs much greater there than for power beamed to locations on Earth. In order to also be able to fulfill the requirements of a Moon base and energy to supply life support, maintenance, communications, and research, a combination of both nuclear and solar energy will be used in the first colonies.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-i2massociates.com-207)

For both solar thermal and nuclear power generation in airless environments, such as the Moon and space, and to a lesser extent the very thin Martian atmosphere, one of the main difficulties is dispersing the [inevitable heat generated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnot_cycle). This requires fairly large radiator areas.

### **Self-replication**

*See also: [von Neumann probe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_probe), [Self-replicating machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-replicating_machine), and [molecular nanotechnology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_nanotechnology)*

[Space manufacturing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_manufacturing) could enable self-replication. Some consider it the ultimate goal because it would allow an [exponential](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exponential_growth) increase in colonies, while eliminating costs to and dependence on Earth.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-214) It could be argued that the establishment of such a colony would be Earth's first act of [self-replication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-replication).[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-215) Intermediate goals include colonies that expect only information from Earth (science, engineering, entertainment) and colonies that just require periodic supply of light weight objects, such as [integrated circuits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrated_circuit), medicines, [genetic material](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA) and tools.

### **Population size**

In 2002, the [anthropologist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthropology) [John H. Moore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_H._Moore) estimated[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-216) that a population of 150–180 would permit a stable society to exist for 60 to 80 generations—equivalent to 2,000 years.

Assuming a journey of 6,300 years, the astrophysicist Frédéric Marin and the particle physicist Camille Beluffi calculated that the minimum viable population for a [generation ship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generation_ship) to reach [Proxima Centauri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxima_Centauri) would be 98 settlers at the beginning of the mission (then the crew will breed until reaching a stable population of several hundred settlers within the ship) .[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-217)[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-218)

In 2020, Jean-Marc Salotti proposed a method to determine the minimum number of settlers to survive on an extraterrestrial world. It is based on the comparison between the required time to perform all activities and the working time of all human resources. For Mars, 110 individuals would be required.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-219)

## Advocacy

*See also: [Space advocacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_advocacy)*

Several private companies have announced plans toward the [colonization of Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonization_of_Mars). Among entrepreneurs leading the call for space colonization are [Elon Musk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk), [Dennis Tito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dennis_Tito) and [Bas Lansdorp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bas_Lansdorp).[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-220)[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-221)

### **Involved organizations**

Organizations that contribute to space colonization include:

- The [National Space Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Space_Society) is an organization with the vision of people living and working in thriving communities beyond the Earth. The NSS also maintains an extensive library of full-text articles and books on space settlement.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-222)
- The [Space Frontier Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Frontier_Foundation) performs [space advocacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_advocacy) including strong [free market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_market), [capitalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalism) views about space development.
- The [Mars Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Society) promotes [Robert Zubrin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Zubrin)'s [Mars Direct](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Direct) plan and the settlement of Mars.
- The [Space Settlement Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Settlement_Institute) is searching for ways to make space colonization happen within a lifetime.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-223)
- [SpaceX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX) is developing extensive [spaceflight transportation infrastructure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX_Mars_transportation_infrastructure) with the express purpose of enabling long-term human settlement of Mars.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-trati20181224-224)[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-sn20181224-225)
- The [Space Studies Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Studies_Institute) funds the study of outer space settlements, especially [O'Neill cylinders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/O%27Neill_cylinder).
- The [Alliance to Rescue Civilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alliance_to_Rescue_Civilization) plans to establish [backups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backup) of human civilization on the Moon and other locations away from Earth.
- The [Artemis Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_Project) plans to set up a private lunar surface station.[[2]](https://ntrs.nasa.gov/archive/nasa/casi.ntrs.nasa.gov/19930008978.pdf)
- The [British Interplanetary Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Interplanetary_Society) promotes ideas for the exploration and utilization of space, including a [Mars colony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Project_Boreas), future propulsion systems (see [Project Daedalus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Project_Daedalus)), terraforming, and locating other habitable worlds.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-226)
    - In June 2013 the BIS began the SPACE project to re-examine Gerard O'Neill's 1970s space colony studies in light of the advances made since then. The progress of this effort were detailed in a special edition of the journal in September 2019.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-:2-227)
- [Asgardia (nation)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asgardia_(nation)) – an organization searching to circumvent limitations placed by [Outer Space Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_Space_Treaty).
- The [Cyprus Space Exploration Organisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus_Space_Exploration_Organisation) (CSEO) promotes space exploration and colonization, and fosters collaboration in space.

## Terrestrial analogues to space settlement

Many [space agencies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_agency) build "testbeds", which are facilities on Earth for testing advanced life support systems, but these are designed for long duration [human spaceflight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_spaceflight), not permanent colonization.

- The most famous attempt to build an analogue to a self-sufficient settlement is [Biosphere 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biosphere_2), which attempted to duplicate Earth's biosphere.
- [BIOS-3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BIOS-3) is another [closed ecosystem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Closed_ecosystem), completed in 1972 in [Krasnoyarsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krasnoyarsk), [Siberia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siberia).[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-228)
- The [Mars Desert Research Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Desert_Research_Station) has a habitat for similar reasons, but the surrounding climate is not strictly inhospitable.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-229)
- [Devon Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devon_Island) [Mars Arctic Research Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flashline_Mars_Arctic_Research_Station), can also provide some practice for off-world outpost construction and operation.[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-230)

## In media and fiction

Although [established space habitats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_stations_and_habitats_in_popular_culture) are a stock element in science fiction stories, fictional works that explore the themes, social or practical, of the settlement and occupation of a habitable world are much rarer.[[*citation needed*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed)]

- [*Solaris*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solaris_(novel)) is noted for its critique of space colonization of inhabited planets. At one point, one of the characters says:[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-231)

We are humanitarian and chivalrous; we don't want to enslave other races, we simply want to bequeath them our values and take over their heritage in exchange. We think of ourselves as the Knights of the Holy Contact. This is another lie. We are only seeking Man. We have no need of other worlds. We need mirrors. (§6:72)

In 2022 [Rudolph Herzog](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudolph_Herzog) and [Werner Herzog](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Werner_Herzog) presented an in-depth documentary with [Lucianne Walkowicz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucianne_Walkowicz) called *Last exit: Space*.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_colonization#cite_note-Machkovech_2022-232)

*"Habitable planet" redirects here. For a list of potentially habitable planets found to date, see [List of potentially habitable exoplanets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_potentially_habitable_exoplanets).*

> 
> 
> 
> Understanding planetary habitability is partly an extrapolation of the conditions on [Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth), as this is the only [planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planet) known to support [life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life).
>
